<div id="review_5152375" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/5152375" />
    <a title="Maria" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/309472-maria"><img alt="Maria" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1535986280p2/309472.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/5152375?book_show_action=true">Aug 26, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maria" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maria" href="/user/show/309472-maria">Maria</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/309472-maria?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer5152375" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6960072678927327616">The mystery here is complex and interesting, and the book has plenty of Lord Peter doing terribly charming and wonderful things, which is always nice, but it is the atmospheric setting of East Anglia, used by Sayers to brilliant effect, that really made the book for me. I nearly cried during the final climactic scene, it was that powerful. <br/><br/>I understand some people don't like that it has so much detail on the history of the bells and change-ringing, but I found it to be just the right amount and </span>
  <span id="freeText6960072678927327616" style="display:none">The mystery here is complex and interesting, and the book has plenty of Lord Peter doing terribly charming and wonderful things, which is always nice, but it is the atmospheric setting of East Anglia, used by Sayers to brilliant effect, that really made the book for me. I nearly cried during the final climactic scene, it was that powerful. <br /><br />I understand some people don't like that it has so much detail on the history of the bells and change-ringing, but I found it to be just the right amount and detail to be interesting, not tedious, and explained well enough to not be absolutely confusing. To me, it added to the dark and brooding atmosphere of the book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6960072678927327616" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer17816609642593230779">An engaging mystery set in Fenchurch St Paul.<br/>Wonderful characters and descriptions of the Church and the art of change ringing.<br/>Beautifully written in the Golden age of crime era.<br/>So of its time.<br/>An engrossing brilliant story.<br/>Will be looking out for more.<br/>A re- read for me!</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_3464735583" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3464735583" />
    <a title="Bruce Beckham" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/28623020-bruce-beckham"><img alt="Bruce Beckham" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442874525p2/28623020.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3464735583?book_show_action=true">Sep 10, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bruce Beckham" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bruce Beckham" href="/user/show/28623020-bruce-beckham">Bruce Beckham</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3464735583" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15027762065371021020">I’m a big fan of period detective stories and this was my first Dorothy L Sayers novel.<br/><br/>I found it to be competently written and pleasant to read or listen to; indeed the literary quality is high, compared to – say – the more workmanlike Agatha Christie.<br/><br/>What I liked most was the setting – the Fenlands of East Anglia, just after the First World War – a fascinating insight into a bleak landscape I know well, and authentically documented. The action centres upon an imposing church with its even more</span>
  <span id="freeText15027762065371021020" style="display:none">I’m a big fan of period detective stories and this was my first Dorothy L Sayers novel.<br /><br />I found it to be competently written and pleasant to read or listen to; indeed the literary quality is high, compared to – say – the more workmanlike Agatha Christie.<br /><br />What I liked most was the setting – the Fenlands of East Anglia, just after the First World War – a fascinating insight into a bleak landscape I know well, and authentically documented. The action centres upon an imposing church with its even more imposing array of curiously named bells, in the small fictional village of Fenchurch St Paul.<br /><br />‘The Nine Tailors’ of the title refers to campanology, and there is quite a lot of it going on, often in minute technical detail; it is an odd quirk – especially in the audiobook!<br /><br />The plot is bafflingly convoluted and unwieldy, while the crimes (or, rather their victims) do not engender a great deal of sympathy. Even Lord Peter Wimsey does not appear hugely motivated, and drifts in and out of the narrative without really getting his teeth into the investigation.<br /><br />I think if you’re seeking a 1920s-style British upper-class sleuth, a robust plot and some emotional engagement, I should go for Margery Allingham’s Albert Campion.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15027762065371021020" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_170897495" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/170897495" />
    <a title="Kim" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4542979-kim"><img alt="Kim" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1454402751p2/4542979.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/170897495?book_show_action=true">May 25, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kim" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kim" href="/user/show/4542979-kim">Kim</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4542979-kim?shelf=crime-fiction">crime-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4542979-kim?shelf=all-time-favourites">all-time-favourites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer170897495" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5023292558931109233">This is a wonderful novel. From the first scenes set in the bleak and snowy Fens countryside, Sayers works her magic. The landscape, the church bells, the superbly-drawn characters and the mystery (well, two mysteries) are expertly woven together to make a supremely satisfying whole. Novels that take the reader to another time and place are, in my opinion, the best novels of all. This one does that for me. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_122386600" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/122386600" />
    <a title="Laura" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/900147-laura"><img alt="Laura" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1544395177p2/900147.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('LH6gYSUReJCk/b5YOxVwPbaiWztqFGhZF7lP2li26kzaHtj7WXATKyhZiwHW56HZff90/4/CL0r9bM2N5JYN6g==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('lTmrxCrNP8vXFdJLqkoiy+9eL0sEZKRzUCxNqFFZ3FdjWdNeVqxUcFux5xJHuPMvJAMAj+Gy42C6+c//7Xk78Q==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<span id="freeTextContainer10777030860190703382">Dorothy Leigh Sayers was a renowned British author, translator, student of classical and modern languages, and Christian humanist.<br/><br/>Dorothy L. Sayers is best known for her mysteries, a series of novels and short stories set between World War I and World War II that feature English aristocrat and amateur sleuth Lord Peter Wimsey. However, Sayers herself considered her translation of Dante's Divina Co</span>
  <span id="freeText10777030860190703382" style="display:none">Dorothy Leigh Sayers was a renowned British author, translator, student of classical and modern languages, and Christian humanist.<br /><br />Dorothy L. Sayers is best known for her mysteries, a series of novels and short stories set between World War I and World War II that feature English aristocrat and amateur sleuth Lord Peter Wimsey. However, Sayers herself considered her translation of Dante's Divina Commedia to be her best work. She is also known for her plays and essays.</span>

            }
            e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});
          });
        });
      $('bookCover_116971').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

//]]>
</script>

</li>
</ul>
</div>

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/2795358-the-nine-tailors">Quotes from The Nine Tailors</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;The bells gave tongue: Gaude, Sabaoth, John, Jericho, Jubilee, Dimity, Batty Thomas and Tailor Paul, rioting and exulting high up in the dark tower, wide mouths rising and falling, brazen tongues clamouring, huge wheels turning to the dance of the leaping ropes. Tin tan din dan bim bam bom bo--tan tin din dan bam bim bo bom--tan dan tin bam din bo bim bom--every bell in her place striking tuneably, hunting up, hunting down, dodging, snapping, laying her blows behind, making her thirds and fourths, working down to lead the dance again. Out over the flat, white wastes of fen, over the spear-straight, steel-dark dykes and the wind-bent, groaning poplar trees, bursting from the snow-choked louvres of the belfry, whirled away southward and westward in gusty blasts of clamour to the sleeping counties went the music of the bells--little Gaude, silver Sabaoth, strong John and Jericho, glad Jubilee, sweet Dimity and old Batty Thomas, with great Tailor Paul bawling and striding like a giant in the midst of them. Up and down went the shadows of the ringers upon the walls, up and down went the scarlet sallies flickering roofwards and floorwards, and up and down, hunting in their courses, went the bells of Fenchurch St. Paul.&rdquo;</span>
